Date:  Tue, 01 Jan 2019 05:50:42 +0000
From:  h2ologg@yahoo.com
Subject:  Video Comet46P from dark Skies
Hi Gang,
My first contribution. Hoping it's worth it.

From Friday Night 2018-12-28. Taken with a SV 80mm refractor an a ZWO 294mc cold camera. The video is a composite of 36 x120sec, 36 x 180sec and 36 x240second light frames and hence the appearance of the comet seeming to loop in the video.

Location shot from my cabin 7700ft, June Lake California, USA with dark steady skies. Comet Wirtanen was obvious in Canon 12 x 36 image stabilizing binos and has been since Dec 8th during the imaging nights.

I will process the frames into a single - if this is of interest. Also I have more frames from Saturday and Sunday Nights, including Comet 38P Stephan-Oterma.

Your group is of inspiration!

Link:
https://www.flickr.com/gp/20313452@N02/pXd5sz https://www.flickr.com/gp/20313452@N02/pXd5sz

Date:  Sat, 05 Jan 2019 22:40:52 +0000
From:  davefriend0@ymail.com
Subject:  46P closes to 11 degrees from 38P
46P/Wirtanen and 38P/Stephan-Oterma will close rapidly during January, then spend all of February less then a dozen degrees apart as they fade away.

Closest approach is 11.3 degrees around Feb.12th for a week.

Should make for some nice photos!

As a DSLR user 12 degrees is the diagonal of the chip in my Canon 700D (T5i) with a 130mm telehphoto.

Or a 200mm lens with a full frame chip like Canon 6D.

Date:  Wed, 09 Jan 2019 19:07:56 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet 64P/Swift-Gehrels (Jan.5,2019)
Object/Date:
64P/Swift-Gehrels @ January 5,2019 21:23 UT

Description:
Comet 64P/Swift-Gehrels imaged on January 5th 2019, three days after a increasing of activity since which has developed a short tail. The green coma has an angular size of 8' and its brightness is near magnitude 8.5. The brightest blue star is 55 Arietis with magnitude 5.7.

Acquisition details:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8.
Camera Atik 383L+.
26 min. total exposure.
>From Vallés, Valencia (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/64p-swift-gehrels-20190105/

Clear and dark skies.

José J. Chambó

Date:  Sun, 13 Jan 2019 19:55:40 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  Comet 46P/Wirtanen (Jan.6,2019)
Object/Date:
46P/Wirtanen @ January 6,2019 02:02 UT

Description:
Comet 46P/Wirtanen photographed early morning on January 6th 2019. Its coma has angular diameter half degree in this image with elongated shape to southwest toward seems there are some tail. Between constellations Lynx and Ursa Major on a field of faint galaxies, the comet has near magnitude 6.

Acquisition details:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8.
Camera Atik 383L+.
37 min. total exposure.
>From Vallés, Valencia (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/46p-wirtanen-20190106/


Clear and dark skies.

Object/Date:
46P/Wirtanen @ January 6,2019 02:02 UT

Description:
Comet 46P/Wirtanen photographed early morning on January 6th 2019. Its coma has angular diameter half degree in this image with elongated shape to southwest toward seems there are some tail. Between constellations Lynx and Ursa Major on a field of faint galaxies, the comet has near magnitude 6.

Acquisition details:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8.
Camera Atik 383L+.
37 min. total exposure.
From Vallés, Valencia (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/46p-wirtanen-20190106/


Clear and dark skies.

Date:  Thu, 17 Jan 2019 03:07:37 +0000
From:  roman.kulesza@hotmail.com
Subject:  Comet 46P/Wirtanen on Jan 14 , 2019
still beautiful.....
Hi , finally I took this comet image from my backyard and with my own telescope :)
It"s cold in Canada - 14 - 18 C and this weekend will be close to - 30 C degrees below zero but I am happy and I"II be able take some pictures of Moon Eclipse .
Last week I cleaned my Newtonian telescope with 10 inch - 254 mm R.F. Royce conical mirror , still need bigger secondary /right now using 2.6 "/
Taken through 10 " inch at F-5 Newtonian and Canon 6D full spectrum modified camera .
30 sub frames 60 second exposure time each stack in DSS and all processing done in MaxIm DSLR V 5
https://www.flickr.com/photos/romanastrophotography/32895486688/in/dateposted-public/ https://www.flickr.com/photos/romanastrophotography/32895486688/in/dateposted-public/

Thanks for looking
Cheers
Roman

Date:  Fri, 18 Jan 2019 10:32:59 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  38P/Stephan-Oterma (Jan.6,2019)
Object/Date:
38P/Stephan-Oterma @ January 6,2019 03:00 UT

Description:
Comet 38P/Stephan-Oterma photographed on January 6, 2019. Going away from inner Solar System shows in this image an asimetric coma with 3' af angular size, whitish and few gassy, which is transform in a dust tail with 15' lenght toward West. Comet had here a brightness near magnitude 10 and located into constellation Lynx, the brightest star has magnitude 7.

Acquisition details:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8.
Camera Atik 383L+.
24 min. total exposure.
From Vallés, Valencia (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/38p-stephan-oterma-20190106/



Clear and dark skies.

José J. Chambó

twitter: @PepeChambo

Date:  Sat, 19 Jan 2019 08:22:24 +0100
From:  rolando ligustri 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] comet C/2018 Y1 Iwamoto, yesterday night
Hi Dr. Clay, let's see if I can answer your request :

the framed field is 26'x39 '
I used a telescope DK 500/2250 with ccd PL6303, RGBfilter
L=3x180 in bin 1
image it's oriented with the N at the top and E to left
tail is oriented about PA284, it's long 8-10'
equalizing the image,coma it's 10 'wide

the tail in the original files is very weak (I could not take more photos, because I found
a free telescope late ...
and the dawn was near) to enhance it I created a mask using an AstroArt plug-in.

regards
Rolando

I think you mean "January 13" not "December 13".Nice shot.
M45 and 64P are closest Jan.22nd & 23rd just 3.5 degrees apart (centre to centre)
6.1 degrees apart in your photo.
They are within 5 degrees Jan.15th to 29th

Date:  Tue, 22 Jan 2019 11:41:52 +1300
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  60P (Tsuchinshan) nice 10' tail
Hi,

I was getting astrometry of comets on 2019 Jan 20 UT with a 41cm f4.5 Meade
Starfinder Newtonian and STF8300M CCD. When doing astrometry of 60P
(Tsuchinshan) I noticed a nice 10' tail. I stacked 10 x 1 minute exposures
and put the image on Spaceweather. Here's the link -

http://spaceweathergallery.com/indiv_upload.php?upload_id=151171

Date:  Sat, 26 Jan 2019 22:04:06 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2018 Y1 Iwamoto (Jan.18,2019)
Object/Date:
C/2018 Y1 (Iwamoto) @ January 18,2019 16:52 UT

Description:
Comet C/2018 Y1 Iwamoto photographed on January 18, 2019 in a image one square degree, shows here a greenish coma of 8' angular size and a small tail 5' long. The comet have here a brightness near magnitude 9.5 and could be seen through binoculars on next February month.

Acquisition details:
Telescope Planewave 20" CDK f/4.4.
Camera FLI-PL09000.
9 min. total exposure.
Remotely from Siding Spring, NSW (Australia).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2018y1-iwamoto-20190118/




Clear and dark skies.

From: mailto:Comet-Images@yahoogroups.com
Sent: Saturday, January 26, 2019 11:04 PM
To: Comet images
Subject: [Comet-Images] C/2018 Y1 Iwamoto (Jan.18,2019)

Object/Date:

C/2018 Y1 (Iwamoto) @ January 18,2019 16:52 UT

Description:

Comet C/2018 Y1 Iwamoto photographed on January 18, 2019 in a image one
square degree, shows here a greenish coma of 8' angular size and a small
tail 5' long. The comet have here a brightness near magnitude 9.5 and could
be seen through binoculars on next February month.

Acquisition details:

Telescope Planewave 20" CDK f/4.4.

Camera FLI-PL09000.

9 min. total exposure.

Remotely from Siding Spring, NSW (Australia).

Post and image link:

http://cometografia.es/2018y1-iwamoto-20190118/

Clear and dark skies.

Jos� J. Chamb�

Date:  Sat, 09 Feb 2019 09:26:29 +0000
From:  martin.mobberley@btinternet.com
Subject:  Re: comet C/2018 Y1 Iwamoto yesterday
Hi Rolando,
I have had this happen to me once or twice. In my case there was a slight difference in the way the R, G and B frames were stretched. I had to go back and make sure the R, G and B frames were processed EXACTLY the same. For some reason on these occasions just a tiny difference in the way one colour channel was stretched made a huge colour difference! It may be that my problem was totally different though! Maybe itel have switched their filters around in that filter wheel?!
Regards,
Martin 
Date:  Sat, 09 Feb 2019 11:15:53 +0100
From:  rolando ligustri 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Re: comet C/2018 Y1 Iwamoto yesterday

uncalibrated files

Date:  Tue, 12 Feb 2019 14:18:52 -0800
From:  thuemen_cm@yahoo.ca
Subject:  Comet C/2018 Y1 (Iwamoto)
Hi All!
A quick check of the files section indicates it’s been almost 10 years since my last confession…Opps…submission. But in those intervening years, I have kept a constant vigil with the group enjoying the visual treats that appear almost daily on this site. For that I thank you! Conditions here in central Canada, along the Ontario-Quebec border, for imaging have been pretty dismal for the last 3 to 4 years. Gone are the cold dry, clear winter nights that would provide diamond filled skies. The only thing that hasn’t changed is the cold nights. It is hard to imagine a frozen fog at –30C…-20F for the fahrenheit crowd, but that is the new normal here. Last evening it was –23C/-10F and frozen percip was persisting so aquiring data for pretty pictures was out of the question. A quick review of a couple of differing exposure durations indicated that Iwamoto was simply flying through Leo, similar to Lulin in 2009…my last submission. So I opted for making a quick video clip to show the movement. Here is the link:

https://groups.yahoo.com/neo/groups/Comet-Images/files/Comet%20C2018%20Y1%20Iwamoto%2C%20The%20Movie/ https://groups.yahoo.com/neo/groups/Comet-Images/files/Comet%20C2018%20Y1%20Iwamoto%2C%20The%20Movie/

The movie clip comprises forty-three 30 seconds images with 1 minute intervals between images for a total time frame of 63.5 minutes…just over an hour. Using Aladin, accessible via the University of Strasbourg website, I was able to get a fairly accurate distance travelled by the comet…16.5 arcminutes. For a reference, the typical full moon is 31 arcminutes so Comet C/2018 Y1 covered just over half the angular width of the moon in just over an hour. That’s pretty quick!!

I hope you enjoy the short clip. Pardon the bit of bounce in the FOV. I was cropping the images to minimize the effect of my mount which needs a bit of polar aligning. Keep those great comet images coming!!

Cheers, Chris.

Date:  Sat, 23 Feb 2019 15:31:58 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2018 Y1 Iwamoto (Feb.10,2019)
Object/Date:
C/2018 Y1 (Iwamoto) @ February 10,2019 04:21 UT

Description:
Comet C/2018 Y1 Iwamoto on February 10th 2019 , three days after its perihelion and three days before ist maximum approaching to Earth. Its ionic tail is faintly visible toward West (to right) in this image, at same time is possible to see a dust tail toeard Southeast (to down-left) only during these days in which our planet cross the orbital plane of comet. The Iwamoto also reached those days its maximum brightness with a magnitude near 6.5 and a coma with angular size of 20'. The brightest star into field is Chi Leonis with magnitude 4.6.

Acquisition details:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8. Camera Atik 383L+. 68 min. total exposure. From Vallés, Valencia (Spain).

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/46p-wirtanen-20190106/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó

twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Date:  Sat, 23 Feb 2019 12:12:25 -0500
From:  Joe Stieber 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] C/2018 Y1 Iwamoto (Feb.10,2019)
Note: The link in the original post went to an image of 46P/Wirtanen. I presume this is the intended image...

http://cometografia.es/2018y1-iwamoto-20190210/

I had observed Iwamoto at the same time, starting at 11:20 pm EST Feb 9 (04:20 UT Feb 10), with 15x56 binoculars from a suburban site in New Jersey (eastern USA) and the coma appeared to partially overlap the brightish, seventh-magnitude star to its left in the picture, HD 95848. Ten minutes later, it was no longer overlapping that star.

Joe Stieber

About a month and a half of cloudy weekends, finally after we got 27 inches of snow, the sky clears.  I sank up to my knees in deep snow last night to trek out to the roll off and get this shot.  The comet is getting fainter fast, so dont wait!  Thanks for looking.

Date:  Tue, 26 Feb 2019 09:51:06 -0600
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] (6478) Gault: a deeper image - 25 Feb. 2019
It was reported in November by several folks speculating about the sudden activity of a main belt asteroid as to whether it had been "hit" by another passing object; that is entirely possible and is one explanation on how so much hitherto unexposed volatile materials could have been exposed to solar radiation to produce the tail(s) that we are seeing. Your point about the longevity of this tail is a good one however; not only the elapsed time with a very consistent narrow and strongly delineated tail, but also the months in which there has been seen very little change in the morphology of the longer tail whatsoever is odd. The secondary shorter tail is something that has emerged just in recent weeks, but the minor planet (6478) itself has yet to show any significant outgassing in terms of coma.....only the pencil-like tail. The minor planet is NOT significantly brighter than it is supposed to be, contrary to early reports of that being the case. It is measured at around 17.3, and the predicted brightness (assuming NO outburst nor impact) has always been within 0.2 or so magnitudes of this; on Feb. 26, the MPC predicted brightness (again not taking into account for any transient activity as we are seeing) was 17.5. So, although we are seeing a rather remarkable development of tail activity, now two, we are not seeing any other cometary activity or nebulosity out of this object.
------------
Dr. Clay

Arkansas Sky Observatories
WEB: www.arksky.org/
FACEBOOK: https://www.facebook.com/groups/421163751426836/

The primary tail extends nearly 5' from the very bright and stellar-like nucleus.

From:  Gianluca Masi 
Subject:  (4678) Gault: "antitail" like feature - 25 Mar. 2019
Dear All,

I'm pleased to share a new image of this very interesting object, grabbed a few
hours ago via the Virtual Telescope robotic facility in Italy.

I see there is a faint feature in the typical "antitail" position, pointing
East, and a more dense structure just West from the object:

https://www.virtualtelescope.eu/2019/03/26/6478-gault-the-double-tailed-asteroid-evolution-25-mar-2019/

Clear skies
Gianluca

Date:  Sun, 12 May 2019 13:02:57 -0600
From:  Alan Hale 
Subject:  Comet Lemmon C/2018 R3
Hello everyone,

Over the past few mornings I have successfully observed this comet on two
occasions at m1 ~13. It is low in the northeastern sky before dawn, and the
viewing geometry gets worse as the comet approaches perihelion, but, it is
there . . .

On May 14 it passes through the northern regions of the Double Cluster (NGC
869 + 884).

Sincerely,
Alan 

Date:  Sun, 12 May 2019 17:32:30 -0500
From:  Bob King 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Comet Lemmon C/2018 R3

Date:  Fri, 19 Jul 2019 22:36:58 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2018 N2 ASASSN (Jul.12, 2019)
Object/Date:
C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) @ July 12,2019 04:11 UT

Description:
Comet C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) was discovered a year ago and will reach perihelion next month of November, but will not go much inside the Solar System and will not shine more higher than magnitude 11. In this image taken on July 12, 2019 the comet is at magnitude 13, have not very gassy appearance but is already showing a nice dust tail. The brightest star is at magnitude 7 highlighting also in upper part the spiral galaxy NGC 1024, the bigest, although at least fifty small galaxies can be seen in this field with only 37 square arcminutes.

Acquisition details:
Telescope Planewave 20" CDK f/6.8
Camera FLI PL09000
Exposure 12.5 min. (L=9x50s bin2 + RGB=2x50s bin3)
>From Slooh Teide Observatory, Canary Islands (Spain)
Processed with Maxim DL and PixInsight

Credits:
Martin VD and Nirmal Paul (obtaining)
José J. Chambó (processing)
Slooh (resources)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2018n2-asassn-20190712/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Date:  Fri, 19 Jul 2019 17:52:44 -0600
From:  Alan Hale 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] C/2018 N2 ASASSN (Jul.12, 2019)
Dear Jose, all,

On this image there is a trailed object, roughly east-west (slightly
east-northeast  west-southwest) a few arcminutes to the NNW of the comet.
Approximate location is 2:38:40 +10:48:50. The MPC¹s object checker does
not list any object at this location at the time you gave for the image. The
trail is faint, but perhaps is slightly diffuse.

Perhaps worth checking out . . .

Sincerely,
Alan

From:  Bob King 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] C/2018 N2 ASASSN (Jul.12, 2019)
Hi Jose and Alan,
Great eye, Alan. That may be something. I double-checked with MegaStar and
went to the magnitude limit using the most obscure galaxy catalog and there
is nothing at that spot. Also, if you look closely, the fuzzy trail shows 5
or 6 small condensations in a row, as if moved during multiple exposures.
Bob

> not list any object at this location at the time you gave for the image.
> The trail is faint, but perhaps is slightly diffuse.
>
> Perhaps worth checking out . . .
>
> Sincerely,
> Alan

On Friday, July 19, 2019, 10:38:13 PM UTC, José J. Chambó jjchambo@hotmail.com [Comet-Images] wrote:

Object/Date:
C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) @ July 12,2019 04:11 UT

Description:
Comet C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) was discovered a year ago and will reach perihelion next month of November, but will not go much inside the Solar System and will not shine more higher than magnitude 11. In this image taken on July 12, 2019 the comet is at magnitude 13, have not very gassy appearance but is already showing a nice dust tail.. The brightest star is at magnitude 7 highlighting also in upper part the spiral galaxy NGC 1024, the bigest, although at least fifty small galaxies can be seen in this field with only 37 square arcminutes.

Acquisition details:
Telescope Planewave 20" CDK f/6.8
Camera FLI PL09000
Exposure 12.5 min. (L=9x50s bin2 + RGB=2x50s bin3)
>From Slooh Teide Observatory, Canary Islands (Spain)
Processed with Maxim DL and PixInsight

Credits:
Martin VD and Nirmal Paul (obtaining)
José J. Chambó (processing)
Slooh (resources)

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2018n2-asassn-20190712/

Clear and dark skies.

José J. Chambóblog:cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambofacebook: JoseJChamboinstagram:@cometografia.

Date:  Thu, 08 Aug 2019 18:45:04 +0000
From:  "José J. Chambó" 
Subject:  C/2018 W2 Africano (Aug.3,2019)
Object/Date:
C/2018 W2 (Africano) @ August 3,2019 02:08 UT

Description:
Comet C/2018 W2 (Africano) imaged on August 3rd 2019. Since my previous images taken a month ago its coma has increased in angular size from 3 to 4 arcminutes. On same period visually observations have reported a brightness gain from magnitude 12 to 11.5. Comet is located on a dense stellar zone between constellation Perseus and Camelopardalis.

Acquisition details:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8.
Camera Atik 383L+.
Exposure 57 min. (L=11x180 bin1 + RGB=4x120 bin2).
>From Hoya Redonda, Valencia (Spain).
Processed with Maxim-DL and PixInsight.

Post and image link:
http://cometografia.es/2018w2-africano-20190803/

Clear and dark skies.

Date:  Mon, 12 Aug 2019 12:31:45 +0000
From:  Jose Chambo 
Subject:  C/2018 W2 Africano (Aug.9,2019)
Object/Date:
C/2018 W2 (Africano) @ August 9,2019 11:03 UT

Description:
Comet C/2018 W2 (Africano) imaged on August 9, 2019 when was passing near star open cluster IC 361, located in Camelopardalis and containing about 60 stars between magnitudes 11 and 18. In this image the external coma appears very faint and with an angular size of only 2 arcminutes, elongated at anti-solar direction (toward west). Visual observations on these date reported the comet with a magnitude arond 11.
​
Acquisition details:
Telescope Planewave 24" CDK f/6.5.
Camera FLI PL09000.
Exposure 9 min. (L=3x120 bin1 + RGB=1x60 bin2).
From Auberry, California (USA).
Processed with PixInsight.

Date:  Sun, 18 Aug 2019 15:53:14 +0000
From:  Jose Chambo 
Subject:  C/2018 N2 ASASSN (Aug.10,2019)
Objeto/Fecha:
C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) @ 10-Agosto-2019 04:32 TU

Descripción:
El cometa C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) fotografiado el 10 de Agosto de 2019 con más resolución. Con un ligero aumento de brillo hasta la magnitud 12.5, su aspecto apenas a cambiado con una coma de 1' que contiene una marcada condensación central y su curvada cola de volvo de más de 5' de longitud.

Datos captura:
Telescopio Planewave 20" CDK f/6.8
Cámara FLI PL09000
Exposición 6.7 min. (L=5x50 bin2 + RGB=1x50 bin3)
Desde Observatorio Slooh Teide, Islas Canarias (España)
Procesado con PixInsight

Créditos:
Martin Vd Dussen y José J. Chambó (obtención)
José J. Chambó (procesado)
Slooh (recursos)

Subject:  C/2017 T2 PANSTARRS (Aug.13,2019)
Object/Date:
C/2017 T2 (PANSTARRS) @ August 13,2019 04:23 UT

Description:
Comet C/2017 T2 (PANSTARRS) imaged on August 13, 2019. With a approximate visual magnitude 13.5 shows a coma still very small with angular size of 0.5 arcminute and a short dust tail with lenght 1.5 arcminutes. This comet could be observable through binoculars on May 2020 with a brightness around magnitude 7.

Acquisition details:
Telescope Planewave 20" CDK f/6.8
Camera FLI PL09000
Exposure 7.5 min. (L=5x50 bin2 + RGB=1x50 bin3)

Subject:  C/2018 W2 Africano (Sep.1,2019)
Object/Date:
C/2018 W2 (Africano) @ September 1,2019 03:31 UT

Description:
2x1 degree panorama with comet C/2018 W2 (Africano) at right showing a diffuse coma with an angular size of 7 arcminutes and a brightness in magnitude 10.5. At left the BFS 31 nebula on ionized hidrogen zone Sh 2-203 barely visible in this image.

Acquisition details:
Telescope GSO 8" N f/3.8.
Camera Atik 383L+.
Mosaic 1x2 tiles.
Exposure 12 min. 2x(L=3x180 bin2 + RGB=1x60 bin3).
>From Hoya Redonda, Valencia (Spain).
Processed with PixInsight.

Date:  Sat, 07 Sep 2019 22:53:29 +0000
From:  Jose Chambo 
Subject:  C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) & 260P/McNaught (Sep.7,2019)
Object/Date:
C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) & 260P/McNaught @ 7-September-2019 10:46 UT

Description:
On September 7, 2019 the comets C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) and 260P/McNaught crossed in the sky on this field sull of small galaxies in Aries constellation. Its minimal angular separation was only 10 arcminutes, although only due our perspective from Earth, as both comets were far away from each other; at bottom comet 260P/McNaught to 0.6 A.U. from us and at upper comet C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) to 2.6 A.U., two times the distance from Earth to Sun separates them.

Acquisition details:
Telescope Planewave 20" CDK f/4.5
Camera FLI PL11002M
Exposure 9 min. (L=3x120 bin2 + RGB=1x60 bin2)
From Mayhill, New Mexico (USA).
Procesed with PixInsight

Credits:
José J. Chambó (www.cometografia.es)

Post and image link:
https://cometografia.es/2018n2-panstarrs-260p-mcnaught-20190907/

Clear and dark skies.

José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

Date:  Mon, 09 Sep 2019 22:07:25 +0700
From:  Mikhail Maslov 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Re: C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) & 260P/McNaught (Sep.7,2019)
Hi all,

I see there is a high attention to the track which intersects the comet
260P and different versions on its nature, so I should clarify that it
is just a satellite. I usually do not remove frames with satellites
tracks from stacking sequences and during initial images checking I
didn't notice that one of them passes directly through the comet 260P,
while after stacking I didn't want to redo all the work just because of
this track, so it remained in the image :)

Best regards,

Mikhail

Date:  Tue, 10 Sep 2019 19:29:05 +0000
From:  Jose Chambo 
Subject:  C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) & 260P/McNaught mono (Sep.7,2019)
Object/Date:
C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) & 260P/McNaught @ September 7,2019 08:44 UT

Description:
Conjunction of comets C/2018 N2 (ASASSN) and 260P/McNaught on September 7, 2019. Photographed with a more sensitive camera than my color image taken at same day, this monochromatic version stand out dust tails details. Highlights inside tail of 260P (at down) is a bright central spine, due we are crossing these days the orbital plane of this comet and we see sideway the most of dust which are always concentrated in that plane.

Acquisition details:
Telescope Planewave 17" CDK f/4.5
Camera FLI PL6303E
Exposure 6 min. (L=3x120 bin2)
>From Mayhill, New Mexico (USA).
Procesed with PixInsight

Post and image link:
https://cometografia.es/2018n2-panstarrs-260p-mcnaught-20190907-mono/

Clear and dark skies.

________________________________
José J. Chambó
blog: cometografia.es
twitter: @PepeChambo
facebook: JoseJChambo
instagram: @cometografia

From:  Jose Chambo 
Subject:  C/2019 Q4 Borisov (Sep.12,2019)
Object/Date:
C/2019 Q4 (Borisov) @ September 12,2019 11:08 UT

Description:
Recent discovered interstellar comet C/2019 Q4 (Borisov) imaged in color on September 12, 2019 at 3.36 AU from Sun its brightness is magnitude 17 showing in this image a size with only 18 arcseconds in which can be observed elongated shaped toward northwest. Analyzing color channel shots seems to me that comet shines more in blue, but I can not confirm it, have to wait some days to achieve more detail.

Acquisition details:
Telescope Planewave 17" CDK f/4.5
Camera FLI PL6303E
Exposure 9 min. (L=3x120 bin2 + RGB=1x60 bin2)
>From Mayhill, New Mexico (USA).
Procesed with PixInsight

Post and image link:
https://cometografia.es/2019q4-borisov-20190912/

Date:  Tue, 17 Sep 2019 13:14:17 +0200
From:  Gianluca Masi 
Subject:  C/2019 Q4: 14 and 17 Sept. 2019
Dear All,

despite the huge lunar interference, its low altitude and the proximity of sunrise, I could imagine this comet on 14 and 17 Sept. from Italy, via the Virtual Telescope Project:

https://www.virtualtelescope.eu/2019/09/14/c-2019-q4-borisov-the-very-likely-first-interstellar-comet-ever-discovered-14-sept-2019/

https://www.virtualtelescope.eu/2019/09/17/c-2019-q4-borisov-the-first-interstellar-comet-ever-discovered-a-image-17-sept-2019/

This morning I saw an hint of coma, despite the severe lunar contamination.

Clear skies
Gianluca

Date:  Mon, 30 Sep 2019 11:09:39 +0000
From:  roman.kulesza@hotmail.com
Subject:  First light with QHY249C
Hi , I would like to share my first light and experience with my new QHY294C cooled cmos camera .
After two months waiting for few adapters I was able take some images .
This is only stack of 40 minutes but different sensitivity is easy visible compare to my astro modified Canon 6D camera.
This new Sony Cmos sensor is so sensitive to H alpha and QE is 75% .
Image was take during bad weather and seeing was under average .
https://www.flickr.com/photos/romanastrophotography/48819846887/in/dateposted-public/ https://www.flickr.com/photos/romanastrophotography/48819846887/in/dateposted-public/

and
https://www.flickr.com/photos/romanastrophotography/48819912282/in/dateposted-public/ https://www.flickr.com/photos/romanastrophotography/48819912282/in/dateposted-public/

I think this camera will be perfect for all Planeatary Nebulae .
Thanks for looking.
Cheers
Roman

From:  D F 
Subject:  Comet Africano only 1.11deg from Neptune Oct. 4.25UT
Some nice photos being taken around the world as comet 2018W2 reaches its brightest (mag 8ish)
On Oct. 04d 06h UT the comet is closest (1.11deg) from Neptune - which would make a nice photo!
Photos to magazine@astronomy.ie please before the comet is too far South from Ireland!
Here's a table (for Ireland 53N,6W) showing when the comet transits, its altitude at that time, and the separation from Neptune:

Date:  Sun, 06 Oct 2019 18:20:15 +0700
From:  Mikhail Maslov 
Subject:  29P on 01.10 with a tail-like feature (Re: [comets-ml] Possible fragmentation event at comet 29P)
Hello,

As my mail to comets-ml seems to be not delivered, I double it here:

This is my image of the comet 29P taken on 01.10. It shows a tail-like
feature going to the down-rignt from the coma. It looks like the dust
expanding along the comet's orbit and could be somehow connected to
fragmentation event or other unusual things happened to the comet.

https://astronomy.ru/forum/index.php?action=dlattach;topic=21075.0;attach=1215248;image

Best regards,

Mikhail Maslov

04.10.2019 2:09, 'Michael S. P. Kelley' msk@astro.umd.edu [comets-ml]
:
Hi everyone,

We've seen a new coma feature at comet 29P that some of us are
interpreting as a fragment or swarm of fragments.� Please see our ATel
for details:

http://www.astronomerstelegram.org/?read=13164

Briefly, the comet is about r=16.0 mag in a small (5" radius)
aperture, and the swarm is 18.4+/-0.1 in the same sized aperture. The
feature is apparent in unprocessed images along a position angle of
~70 deg, 7 to 9 arcsec away.

Cheers,
msk

Date:  Sat, 12 Oct 2019 10:42:47 +0200
From:  astro 
Subject:  Almost 21000 comet images in the gallery of the German Comet Section
Hi,

I'm the maintainer of the image gallery of the German Comet Section.
http://fg-kometen.vdsastro.de/fgk_hpe.htm

We are getting close to the 21000 image.

The gallery contains images from 944 comets, several in multiple
apparations.

The oldest image is from comet C/1967 Y1 Ikeya-Seki.

You can search the database for a particular comet image.
http://fg-kometen.vdsastro.de/pix/test/fg-suche_e.php

Everybody is invited to upload his comet images. If you want to upload
older images feel free to contact me by email.

Let me know if you have ideas to enhance the image gallery.

Clear skies,

--

Stefan Beck

"Astrophotography with small telescopes"
http://www.cometchaser.de

"Bildbearbeitung für Kometen"
http://www.cometchaser.de/imageprocessingcomets_de_v3.html

"Image processing for Comets"
http://www.cometchaser.de/imageprocessingcomets_v3.html

Date:  Thu, 17 Oct 2019 19:12:00 +0000
From:  kodama@alumni.caltech.edu
Subject:  Special Notice!: Comet-images group migration
This notification is to make you aware that the Yahoo Comet-Images group - https://groups.yahoo.com/neo/groups/Comet-Images/info https://groups.yahoo.com/neo/groups/Comet-Images/info - is affected by Yahoo's downsizing of its group hosting. Yahoo's info is here: https://help.yahoo.com/kb/groups/SLN31010.html?impressions=true https://help.yahoo.com/kb/groups/SLN31010.html?impressions=true

In summary, the group communications will be maintained, for an undetermined time, purely as an email distribution. Yahoo will not be hosting past messages or images. An option for an email digest will also not be available. As of October 28, 2019, group messages and images will not be updated with new posts. Older posts and images will be available only until Dec. 14. If you have uploaded any images or files and want to save them, download them before the Dec. 14 deadline.

A "refugee" camp is being set up at: https://groups.io/g/comet-images https://groups.io/g/comet-images

This group is likely to become a permanent location for this group. Some of the reasons for this choice:

- Availability of a free account level, both for the group hosting and individual users
- Good feature set - options for email only, web browsing, searching, etc.
- Apparent satisfaction of other former Yahoo groups which have migrated there

A limitation of this service at the free level is very limited space for images and/or attachment files - 1GB total. Most people who have been posting in our group have simply posted links to externally hosted images. This will be even more important at the groups.io location.

Reasons why some other services were not selected:

- Facebook - very polarized user reactions to the service, abrupt service term changes
- Google groups - questionable longevity of the service
- MeWe - very "distracting" user experience

If you have some feedback (especially alternative services to consider), please reply on this thread (on Yahoo), or simply subscribe on the new group:

https://groups.io/g/comet-images/join https://groups.io/g/comet-images/join

All current members of this group will get an invitation today, so you can just wait for that if you'd like and vote your approval/disapproval by signing up or not.

If you choose to create a group on an alternative host, please let us all know too.

Thanks again for participating and especially for keeping this group focused (on comets) and civil.
